Worst Karaoke place ever! So recently my friend got into an accident and she couldn't show up. However, we reserved the room for 7 people and we had to pay for the extra person. How hard is it to show a sense of humanity and just deduct $14 from the bill? I would understand if my friend showed up and left but she couldn't even show up because of a huge car accident. Do you expect her to crawl out of the hospital and go there???  Worst customer service ever too, the person that picked up when we called, showed no respect what so ever. Service here sucks too. They make people pay an unreasonable amount for tip even though, they do absolutely NOTHING. They also have hidden fees that aren't upfront and you don't realize until you pay. ALSO, the playlist software is EXTREMELY annoying. Yes, the song selection would've been nice if you were still stuck in the early 2000s. How is this place still in business? < Review>
3.5 stars~ energy was touted as one of the nicer KTV in SoCal, and while it has a modern veneer I unfortunately found song selection lacking. The rooms are nice and clean and I liked the iPad system. The service was also great with an employee taking drink orders and consistently checking to see if everything was working.

Most of the old music videos were actually accurate and decent, though a few did have the standard "woman walking around foreign country." I just wish they organized the system so it's easier to find newer songs. The highlight was definitely the service, they adjusted room temperature, took care of drinks, and were generally friendly.< /Review>

<Date>1589296257237</Date><userid>109721331336218138310</userid>< Text>
We have used this park in some way everyday since it opened approximately ten years ago. It‚Äôs not big enough for such a large community and it really should have included the land that is now the elementary school to make it a proper park. The lawn is well maintained but the replanting of annuals and perennials is spotting. They recently started to plant cactus and it looks wrong in a family park; not inviting. As mentioned, the poorly thought out Cal Aero school is adjacent to the park and because developers did not give enough land to the playground, the children have PE in the park during the school week, making it hard for residents to lounge and enjoy the park quietly. Also, because they didn‚Äôt build enough permanent structures for the school, they built trailers for extra classrooms. Now the park‚Äôs aesthetics is thrown off and anyone walking along the south end of the park gets a view of trailers and the dirty backside of the school. It just amazes me that in this newer development, these details weren‚Äôt thought out better.< /Text>

<Date>1600988779837< /Date><rating>5</rating>< Text>
I just completed my second FUT procedure at Bosley yesterday.  Both of which were carried out by the real world-class master Dr. Deutsch and I cannot say how happy I am with the results.  I am ecstatic in fact.

My battle with baldness began in my 30s.  Considerable hair loss in front area with my hairline disappearing.  So I had my first operation by dear Dr. Deutsch in 2007 who completely reconstructed a very natural and beautiful hairline for me.

Ten years later I desired more hair density in the same area of my head and I was talked into traveling to Turkey by a family member who told me that the work in that country was good and the price very inexpensive.  The clinic in Turkey where I did my second procedure had all the great reviews and the price was very reasonable.  1800‚Ç¨ For 1300 grafts.  So I went ahead with it and boy did I regret doing so afterwards.

The Dr. in Turkey utterly destroyed my beautiful hairline and completely didn't do what I had asked him for.  They put hairs in places that I hadn't asked them to and didn't put hairs in areas that I wanted it in.  A complete mess.  What was even more annoying was that I noticed their mistakes immediately a day after the operation when I was going through recovery.  HELL!  A nightmare.  My hair looked worse than prior to the first time I had had the operation

So I returned to Bosley and Dr Deutsch did a really wonderful job and I cannot convey how happy I am today.  Not only that but he also did an additional 400 grafts for me absolutely free.  What a result.

I come from a family of four generations in hair and beauty business internationally.  I work between Europe and US and thus come across many people who deal with hair in general.

By far Bosley is the best in the world.  You may be able to get your hair restored cheaper elsewhere but DO NOT waste you money and time.

With Bosley not only you receive the best service but also most importantly you receive the artistry which is second to none.  The results are natural and crucially complimentary to the shape of your face rather than a generic method made the same for everyone.

Their team were putting effort into each individual graft.  Placing them so that they would have the most beautiful impact.  Other places can grow hair for you but they plant them randomly like a messy garden but Dr. Deutsch and team I would compare to landscape gardeners who know where each individual graft must go.

In short I don't think there is anything better to spend your money on than to get your hair back.  We buy many precious things in life but nice hair is something that we can enjoy every single day of our lives and we literally take it to the grave with us so why take a chance when you can have the most advance technology and expertise at Bosley.

All the other staff who were working on me at time of my procedure were totally dedicated to me, extremely helpful and caring.

Thank you Dr. Deutsch, thank Bosley and the staff.  I hope you go from strength to strength.

Korosh</Text>

But right from the beginning, she had a grouchy attitude with me and was stand-offish through the remainder of the day with me. The doctor then came in to confirm my purchase and said, "I see we're doing 1,000 grafts..." I said, "No, I'm supposed to have 1100." He said, "Oh well we need to change your plan because that's extra." So we argued briefly and he then said that yes it's 1100 but it's 100 free, but if I want more we have to charge more. Anyway, the surgeon was argumentative with me when all I was trying to do was confirm the 1100 that I was supposed to have. This interaction affected our rapport for the remainder of the procedure and I felt very uncomfortable even being operated on by him or his grouchy MA. Also, the vibe in the room made me feel like it was a burden to staff when I asked for more snacks or drinks; if would often take a long time to get more water or a drink. Then, as the snack wrappers would pile up on my tray next to me, no one ever removed them for me or offered to do so. <Date>1516149009359< /Date><response>{'time': 1516203756423, 'text': 'Thank you for sharing Michael!  What a great experience!  Steve, Dr. Deutsch, Latoya, Michelle, and the entire Beverly Hills Team will be happy to hear your feedback!  We look forward to working with you in the future!  Thanks again for sharing!'}< /response>< Review>
My entire experience with Bosley was amazing.  For reference, I did the FUE procedure, 2433 grafts but who‚Äôs counting?  My story:

I‚Äôve had thinning hair since the end of high school... I remember a friend joking I should go to Bosley when I wasn‚Äôt even out of college.  I know how it feels to see terrible thinning in every photo - it sucks.

About 6 months ago I decided to look into finally doing hair restoration.  I started by going to Ziering.  I left unimpressed by the entire experience.

Cut to December 2017... I received a gift card offer from Bosley and it reminded me I‚Äôd never gone to Bosley for a consultation (after what I saw at Ziering I saw no point).  Fortunately I had free time to kill so I thought, why not?

My appt was for January 2nd.  I met with Steve Costomiris who was amazing.  I immediately felt at ease and appreciated his dry sense of humor.  He took time to take photos of me and found past patients with similar balding patterns which personalized the experience.  I left feeling I wanted to do the procedure but still a little hesitant (mostly over cost but also a bit nervous about pain).

That night I emailed Steve and he immediately began working with me to address my concerns.  We agreed to talk the next day.

Next day rolls around - Steve had addressed all my concerns and told me there had been a cancelation for the following day.  I immediately booked it.

Cut to day 3 - I arrived early.  Steve greeted me and introduced me to Dr. Deutsch (also a great guy).  We went over the plan for the procedure, he answered my questions and it was off to the procedure room.

I met the team that would be working on me that day (and by day, I mean day... it‚Äôs a long procedure).  I will never forget Latoya who took the time to put me at ease and basically reassure me that everything would be ok.  We took care of initial setup, Michelle came in and numbed my head and we were off and running.

The initial shots were a little painful but they do their best to mitigate that with a massage device.  Once numb, however, I felt no pain at all.  They spent a few hours harvesting hairs, brought me a sandwich that was so delicious I‚Äôm probably driving back to Beverly Hills to eat at that deli again (Lazy Daisy, I believe).

After lunch it was time to plant the hairs - given the size of the job the next ~3-4 hours I was watching TV, chatting, and having the procedure continue.  They were so professional they could SEE the numbness was wearing off somehow and asked to make sure I was still comfortable.  Fortunately they did because I thought I could make it through but I definitely felt that re-numbing shots (moral of that story is don‚Äôt be a hero - ask for reinforcement of the numbing agent when you start to feel it or you‚Äôll be sorry later).

Near the end of the procedure Steve popped in to check on it and see how it went.  Shared a few laughs and then they finalized the last hairs on my head.

Latoya went over how to care for the precious hairs - each one a fancy Starbucks drink (that‚Äôs how I look at it).  Dr. Deutsch showed me with a mirror what we were able to accomplish and then Latoya walked me out, implored me to call if I needed anything at all, and then ‚Äî best of all ‚Äî gave me a big hug goodbye.

All in all, I‚Äôm thrilled I finally did this.  I wish I‚Äôd done it sooner.  Based on the hairline I started with and what I want to end up with I may need a 2nd procedure next year.  I‚Äôm looking forward to it and seeing everybody again.

Do yourself a favor and don‚Äôt wait - at least get the consultation.</Review>

Very professional environment and great service, highly recommended!<//review>

< review>
Go to Subway if you want to have a memorable and (if you'll relax a minute and enjoy the ride) fun experience buying a guitar from someone who gets guitars. It seems people prefer homogeneity over character these days, I think it's a shame. Subway is a great little community fixture. Unpretentious, laid-back, and they won't sell you things you don't need or that don't suit your needs. Go to Guitar Center if you want the box-store approach, or you want to be lied to or misled for the sake of them making a sale. Subway will buy back your guitar and there's a 2-week try-anything policy. Very cool.<//review>

<Review>I haven't been there in nearly 30 years as I live in Maine and don't get to CA anymore. However, I visited there once  and ordered a 9 string guitar! It was made from NOS parts and featured a Danelectro long horn body and Silvertone neck. It had a single coil in the neck position and a humbucker with coil splitting in the bridge. The extra strings were double course on the G, B, and E strings. I had it for a few years and finally traded it although I probably should have kept it. They did a good job assembling it; it just didn't sit very well in my lap. But if you want a cool one of a kind guitar, these guys can build it for you!</Review><Pictures>None< /Pictures>< response>

< text>
Interesting shop, but their inventory is mostly busted up / Frankensteined guitars on the walls and literal piles of beautiful classics that are rotting away in forgotten cases. I went in looking for an older pre-60's Gibson and was given a lot of lip about, "Do you even have the money for this guitar?" It's a frustrating experience to see so many guitars that could use a good home sitting latent in a dusty pile while the owner brags about this only being a fraction of his collection and Lords his own mystique over you.

If you can see through the Berkeleyness of the shop, you can presumably conduct business in this shop, but expect to pay collector prices for unkempt dogs.</text>

<Rate>4< /Rate>< Review>
I can't decide whether it's great or shocking or ?? that a place like this can still exist in the 21st century... from a business standpoint it's a mess (the guy who helped me didn't seem to know where anything was, not surprising given the chaos of their nonexistent filing system), and the ambience is definitely vintage stoner (the guy did take time to talk to me about what needed doing to the guitar, which was nice). I was a little dubious of whether they'd ever be able to find my guitar again, let alone perform the service needed within a reasonable time frame, but amazingly, he called me two days later and told me it was ready to pick up, and they did a good job for a very reasonable price, so clearly something's going right. They also let me take the guitar trusting that I would mail them a check because I didn't have enough cash (which was unnecessarily nice of them) and because they don't take credit cards (sweetly vs frustratingly (?) antiquated). I mailed them the check the same day, and it was cashed shortly thereafter, but they just called me to ask whether I had mailed them the check yet, so, again, see comments above re: the filing system. Not the usual bright shiny Customer Shopping Experience you get at more upmarket places, but definitely a breath of fresh air in its own grubby eccentric way ;) Recommend to anyone who dislikes shopping malls.<//Review>
